Hi Netperf community!!

I wonder why so many people suddenly unsubscribe from this list, although
it's such a nice one ;-))

However, my name is Heico Salfeld, and I worked on an extension of an
existing ATM testbed in order to run ATM traffic over a Eutelsat satellite
link which is leased by the European Space Agency (ESA).

I was using this "real" satellite link (2 Mbps, transparent) as a loopback,
thus all data sent to the satellite is sent back from the satellite to our
own Ground Station. Then I analyzed the throughput using "Netperf" . I was
analyzing the performance of Classical IP and LAN Emulation running on our
FORE equipment.
(See attached file: loopback_scenario.jpg)

For the ATM testbed I am using a number of FORE equipment, like several ATM
NICs (inside a Digital Alpha server 4100 and a NT Workstation PC), an ATM
Switch ASX200BS with OC3, E1 and E3 modules (and an Ethernet switch ES-3810
which is not used in my setup) . For the interfacing between the ATM switch
and the satellite modem I used a COMSAT ALA-2000 (ATM Link Accelerator). I
don't know if anyone is familiar with this ALA-2000 from COMSAT, but
basically it is doing conversion from ATM E3 to RS449 and Reed-Solomon
Coding, and data compression.

When analyzing Classical IP and LANE, I measured a maximal throughput of less
than 1 Mbps like usual on satellite links with a RTT of 540ms and a standard
TCP window size of only 64 kBytes (well-known TCP over satellite issue). Of
course, this is normal.

I was measuring the throughput depending on the TCP window size which was
changed by the Netperf software (params -s and -S for receiver's buffer
size). As attachments I send you a graph showing the measured throughputs of
Classical IP (yellow), LAN Emulation (red) and the maximal throughput
possible for that size of TCP window (blue):
(See attached file: LANEvsCIPoverSat.jpg)

For the Classical IP you can see a "stepwise increase" of the throughput as a
function of TCP window size. For LANE you can see a rather constant increase.
I could not find any explaination for that "phenomenon". I also tried other
MTU sizes for Classical IP than the default 9180 Bytes (32kB and 64kB) and
you can see these results in the following figure:
(See attached file: CIPoverSat.jpg)

I am wondering why I get the stepwise increase of throughput for Classical IP
over satellite as a function of TCP window size. I don't think that this is
because of a mis-configuration of Clasical IP. Maybe somebody could have an
idea ?

Best Regards,
Heico Salfeld
ESA-ESTEC
